Shao Peizi No Longer to Head Zhejiang University

No One Responsible for University Affairs to This Day

Shao Peizi, the president of Zhejiang University, was forced to resign from his position last month due to criticism from students. He submitted his resignation five times in writing and once in person, but none were approved. After being unable to return to Hangzhou, Shao focused on managing the College of Liberal Arts and Sciences, as his resignation only pertained to the position of university president and not to the position of dean of the College of Liberal Arts and Sciences. Since submitting his resignation, Shao has not been seen at Zhejiang University. Currently, university affairs are being handled independently by each college, and everything is proceeding as usual. A few weeks ago, students destroyed the provincial party headquarters. Li Ximou, the dean of the College of Engineering, and Xu Xuan, the dean of the College of Science, submitted their resignations to the central government, with Shao also being listed. However, the Ministry of Education issued instructions that these were unnecessary and ordered President Shao to inform the deans of the colleges. From this, it can be seen that the central government never approved Shao's resignation. However, Shao insisted vehemently and refused to resume the position of university president.

Local News

Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee Decides to Establish University Scholarship

The Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee held its eighth meeting of the Chinese delegation at 408 Avenue Albert. The committee members present were Chu Minyi, Zeng Zongjian, Li Zhaohuan, Zhu Shijin, and Lei Xiaocen. Those present were Secretary Liu Xichang and Assistants Nong Ruhui and Tian Shoucheng. Chu Minyi chaired the meeting. First, the chairman reported on a letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs notifying the reorganization of the Belgian delegation and the list of members after the reorganization, as well as the work of the Standing Committee of the Committee. Then, the meeting discussed the plan to establish a university thesis scholarship, which was proposed by Committee Member Li Zhaohuan. The plan proposed that the Chinese delegation allocate three thousand yuan annually to solicit essays on designated topics and award scholarships to those with outstanding achievements. However, this scholarship is limited to students of domestic universities. The regulations and detailed rules for the thesis scholarship were revised and approved by the delegation meeting. The Committee also decided to host a banquet for scientific experts at the Hua'an Restaurant on January 3, 1932, and invite the experts to propose essay topics for public announcement. Next, the meeting discussed a letter from Cai Yuanpei proposing to invite the Belgian scholar Professor Paul Otlet to give lectures in China and to send Tan Xihong to give lectures in Belgium. This was approved. Finally, the meeting discussed a letter from Various Forces requesting subsidies. It was resolved that the Committee's funds for this year had already been fully allocated and that the matter would be submitted to the general meeting next year for discussion. The regulations and detailed rules for the Committee's university thesis scholarship are excerpted as follows:

Regulations of the Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee for University Thesis Scholarships Article 1: To encourage academic research, the Committee will allocate three thousand yuan annually as thesis scholarships for students of Chinese universities. Article 2: The scholarship is divided into several types, each with several grades. The Committee will announce essay topics and select those with genuine insights and value, awarding them scholarships based on the evaluation results. Article 3: Applicants for this scholarship must be graduating students of legally registered domestic universities or independent colleges. Their theses must be related to their major fields of study. Article 4: The types and categories of theses and the allocation of scholarships will be determined annually by the Chinese delegation of the Committee before the solicitation of essays. Article 5: The Committee will temporarily invite experts to form a committee to handle the thesis topics and evaluations. Article 6: The theses can be written in Chinese, English, German, or French. Article 7: If, after the committee members have reviewed the theses, they believe that none are worthy of a certain type or grade of scholarship, the Chinese delegation of the Committee may retain that type or grade of scholarship as an accumulation for the scholarship fund. Article 8: The above-mentioned accumulated funds may be used by the Committee, but only for the purpose of encouraging academic research. Article 9: Detailed rules for the implementation of these regulations will be formulated separately. Article 10: These regulations may be amended by the Chinese delegation of the Committee.

Provisional Detailed Rules for the Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee's University Thesis Scholarships Article 1: In accordance with Article 1 of the Regulations of the Committee for University Thesis Scholarships, the scholarship is tentatively divided into six types, each with three grades: Grade A, three hundred yuan; Grade B, one hundred and fifty yuan; and Grade C, fifty yuan. The Committee will award the scholarships according to the results of the thesis evaluation. Article 2: The Committee will designate six departments from among the departments specified in Article 6 of the University Regulations of the Ministry of Education each year in rotation. It will invite experts to propose topics to be announced for essay solicitation before February 1. Article 3: Each thesis must be submitted to the Secretariat of the Committee by the president of the university or the dean of the independent college before May 15 of the same year, along with a written certificate stating the author's name, place of origin, age, gender, class, department, and the name and academic qualifications of the supervisor. Article 4: The Committee will invite experts and members of the Chinese delegation of the Committee to form a Thesis Evaluation Committee based on the nature of the designated departments. Article 5: The Thesis Evaluation Committee must submit the evaluation results along with all the theses to the Chinese delegation of the Committee for review and announcement within one month of receiving the theses. Article 6: A list of reference books must be attached to the thesis. If Chinese is used, detailed annotations of the original terms should be included. Article 7: In addition to the scholarships stipulated in Article 1, the Committee may also award honorary awards. Article 8: Each scholarship and each honorary award will be sent by the Chinese delegation of the Committee to the school of the awardee for distribution. Article 9: Each winning thesis will be published by the Committee. Article 10: All theses, whether they win an award or not, will not be returned. Article 11: If there are any matters not covered in these detailed rules, the Chinese delegation of the Committee may amend them at any time.

Chen Mingshu Expresses Apology to Shanghai Student Union for the January 18th Tragedy

(Zhonghua News Agency) After the tragic January 18th incident occurred during the demonstration in Beijing by students from various universities in this city, all the students returned to Shanghai. The Anti-Japanese United Association of University Students decided to send two representatives from each school to form a delegation to negotiate in Beijing. In addition to making requests regarding internal affairs and foreign affairs, the delegation also requested that the government express its apology to the people regarding the tragedy. Now, the delegation has returned to Shanghai on the 27th. Regarding the government's apology to the people, Chen Mingshu, the commander of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison, has expressed his apology in writing. The original letter is recorded as follows: To the Shanghai Student Delegation, Greetings. This student movement arose purely from patriotic enthusiasm. The government has always maintained order with the intention of cherishing the youth, which has been understood by all students. However, due to the congestion of people at the time, Mr. Yang Tongheng was unfortunately pushed into the water and died, which has been verified by the court. The coffin has been prepared with due respect. Mr. Yang suffered a tragic death due to his public service, and the government has a responsibility for not providing adequate protection. We express our deep sorrow and regret after the incident. Therefore, we send this special letter to express our apology. We hope for your understanding. Sincerely, Chen Mingshu, Commander of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison.

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute and the Professional Interaction Society held their fourth service talk yesterday, with over eighty people attending. West YMCA Basketball Championships Next Week

Hujiang Has the Best Chance in Group A

Huzhong and Chenxing Clash in Group B

—Yesterday, Xia Guang Wins, and Jinan Beats Yue Han—

The West YMCA basketball tournament has been going on for a month and a half. Currently, in Group A, Hujiang, Mai Ling, and Haizhe are undefeated. The championship is contested among these three teams. Next week (the eighth week) is the final week of competition, and the matches in each group are extremely important. For example, Hujiang vs. Haizhe and Mai Ling vs. Haizhe are key to the championship and are truly worth watching. The results of yesterday's three matches show that the match between Xia Guang and Jinan was more intense. Results from each match (1) You Tai beats Tongwen (B) 50-10 (2) Xia Guang beats Jinan in Group A 40-34 (3) Yue Han beats Ye Shi in Group A 44-33

Xia Guang beats Jinan During the first half, Jinan's star players Huang Zhaolin and Cai Rongrui did not enter the court, so no one scored. Xia Guang sailed smoothly and won the first half 22-11. In the second half, Jinan's Huang and Cai worked hard and repeatedly scored, gradually approaching the score. They once exceeded Xia Guang 29-27, but like a flash in the pan, they were immediately overshadowed by Xia Guang. Although Jinan tried hard again, Xia Guang was heavily guarded, and it was difficult to achieve anything. As a result, Xia Guang won 45-34.

Yue Han beats Yeshi At the beginning of the Yue Han vs. Yeshi match, Yue Han took the lead. Yeshi was unwilling to be outdone, working together to resist. The situation was quite tense, and the score was once tied at 14-14. Yue Han reorganized its army, demonstrating its ambition and winning the first half 17-14. After a break and re-battle, Yue Han's Miao Lianen and Cheng Jingxing scored nine points in a row, increasing their momentum. Yeshi fought hard, and Tong Wenyuan made many contributions. Both sides fought fiercely, giving excellent performances. As a result, Yue Han won 44-33.

Mayor Zhang Qun's Resignation Approved

Chen Mingshu Concurrently Appointed as Successor

Since the Mayor of this city, Zhang Qun, repeatedly submitted his resignation to the Central Government due to the aftermath of the war, all sectors of this city have repeatedly telegraphed to urge him to stay. The Central Government has also twice comforted Mayor Zhang and did not approve his resignation. However, Zhang's determination to leave was firm. He personally expressed his difficulties to the Central Government during his attendance at the First Plenary Session of the Fourth National Congress and resolutely requested to retire. It is now learned that the Central Government has understood his situation and has approved his resignation. As for the successor, it is rumored that the Central Government has internally appointed Chen Zhenru, the Commander of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison, to concurrently hold the position. Once the official order is issued, the handover can be carried out.

Songhu Garrison Commander Dai Ji Takes Office Today

Oath Ceremony Scheduled to be Held Later

The newly appointed Songhu Garrison Commander, Dai Ji, was originally scheduled to take office yesterday. However, due to the incomplete handover procedures at various locations, it was rescheduled to this morning. Yesterday morning around 10:00 AM, Dai sent Chief of Staff Zhang Xiang, along with responsible personnel from various departments, to the headquarters. The former Chief of Staff of the headquarters, Xu Jinyuan, handed over the official seal and important documents to Zhang for acceptance. Xu Yiheng received the General Office, Lai Weiying received the Staff Office, Lin Jin received the Adjutant Office, Chen Hanzuo received the Military Law Office, Zhuang Weigang received the Quartermaster Office, Qiu Xian received the Investigation Team, and Zheng Shizhen received the Medical Office. The handover was completed at 3:00 PM in the afternoon. There have been slight changes in the internal personnel. It is rumored that Xu Yiheng has been internally appointed as the Director of the General Office, Lai Weiying (original position) as the Chief of the Staff Office, Lin Jin as the Chief of the Adjutant Office, Zhuang Weigang as the Chief of the Quartermaster Office, Chen Hanzuo (current Presiding Judge of the Military Law Joint Trial in this city) as the Chief of the Military Law Office, and Qiu Xian as the Chief of the Investigation Team. However, the Director of the Medical Office has not been determined. A reporter from this newspaper interviewed Chief of Staff Zhang Xiang yesterday, who stated that the original Chief of the Adjutant Office, Jiang Yi, will be transferred to another position. Commander Dai has determined to take office tomorrow (i.e., today) due to the importance of the Songhu security, and an oath of office will be held at a later date. It is heard that the oath-taking date has been tentatively set for the 31st.

Disturbances Occurred at the Shanghai West Daxin Dyeing Factory Yesterday

Factory Forces Workers to Leave

All Workers Held a Major Petition Yesterday

The Daxin Dyeing Factory on Binlang Road, Xiaoshadu, Shanghai West, announced its closure on October 19th due to problems with raw materials. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau mediated several times without success and submitted it to the Municipal Government for arbitration. All the workers still lived in the factory. Yesterday morning, the factory forcibly drove the workers out, causing disturbances. The various situations are recorded as follows:

Forced to Leave Factory: At 9:00 AM yesterday, the Daxin Factory requested two armed Chinese detectives and Western constables from the Gordon Road Police Station to forcibly drive all the workers out of the factory. Worker representative Li Renkang and others explained to the Chinese detectives, but the police refused to accept and ordered everyone to leave the factory within five minutes. All the workers refused to leave because they had not received orders from the labor union. At 10:30 AM, the police station sent more than 40 armed Chinese and Western detectives to forcibly drive them out of the factory. At that time, the workers Yang Fuqing, Xu Shiqing, Zhu Xiangyun, and others were seriously injured, and workers Xie Shengxiang and others were slightly injured.

Collective Petition: Yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, all the workers used removal trucks to transport more than 20 workers who had been seriously and slightly injured to the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters of the Chinese Nationalist Party on Lin Yin Road, West Gate, and held a large-scale petition, demanding (1) that the factory immediately resume operations, (2) that the instigators Shao Zhongying and Que Pingzhi be severely punished, and (3) that the dead be given preferential treatment, and the injured be compensated for medical expenses and all losses. Zhou Lianze of the Civil Training Section received them and promised to accept their demands completely. Subsequently, they went to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to petition.

Injuries: The injured workers Yang Fuqing, Xu Shiqing, Zhu Xiangyun, and others were sent to Nanyang Hospital, South Gate, by the Municipal Party Headquarters. It is heard that Yang's injuries are in the lungs and abdomen and are quite serious, and his life is in danger. Xu's injury is in the waist and is also quite serious, but there may be no danger to his life. Zhu's injury is in the head and is not very serious. The slightly injured worker Xie Shengxiang returned to seek medical treatment on his own.

Emergency Meeting: The Silk Guang Office of the Dyeing Industry Labor Union, in response to the violent and illegal expulsion and beating of workers at the Daxin Factory, has specifically scheduled an emergency meeting of all silk and Guang factory workers in the city at the Luban Road Silk Guang Office at 6:00 PM today to discuss countermeasures.

Labor Union Declaration: To all labor unions in the city, it is a fact that the Daxin Silk Guang Dyeing Factory, which opened on Binlang Road, Xiaoshadu, announced its closure on October 19th due to a lack of raw materials. At that time, our union, based on the factory's letter, believed that although raw materials from Japanese goods were being boycotted, there were still domestically produced yarns to supply, and it was also possible to use goods from the United Kingdom and the United States for relief. There was absolutely no way to actually announce the closure. Moreover, at this time of national crisis, all citizens should resist the violence of Japan with all their strength, especially those engaged in industry and commerce, who should strive to develop production and fundamentally eliminate enemy goods from the market. Therefore, our union requested the factory to resume operations with the utmost enthusiasm. Workers were willing to voluntarily reduce wages and increase work to help the factory reduce its economic burden. In the industrial sector, it can also increase production and development, which is beneficial to both the country and the people. Our union comforted the factory with the utmost sincerity. Unexpectedly, the factory did not understand the workers' difficulties and used the lack of raw materials as an excuse, and also cited the losses in business over the years. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau did not thoroughly investigate the facts of the factory's closure and only discussed giving workers money to dissolve the factory. Our union, under the oppression of the factory and the lack of government protection, still instructed all the workers in the factory to maintain order and await the assistance of the Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government's legal arbitration. Unexpectedly, since February, while the Party and government authorities were conducting a thorough investigation and handling the matter, the factory intensified its actions. Yesterday, it hired dozens of detectives, armed with live ammunition, and ordered all the workers in the factory to be driven out. The workers of the factory refused to leave the factory until the government had properly planned a solution, which led to a major incident. Workers Yang Fuqing and others were seriously injured all over their bodies and were on the verge of death. Now, our union, in addition to fighting to the death, requests the Party and government authorities to quickly plan proper solutions for the dead and injured workers and immediately order the factory to resume operations. We also hope that all friendly associations in the city will give us their full assistance so that we can achieve our goals. We would be extremely grateful. This declaration is hereby made.

Rihua Factory Workers Petition Today

Held a General Meeting Yesterday to Discuss the Approach

Welcome the Arrested Workers Back to the Workshop

After all the workers in the Rihua Yarn Factory cloth machine room in Pudong went on strike, the Japanese colluded with ruffians to forcibly refuse to resume work and continued to suppress and dismiss a large number of workers for no reason. Yesterday, the workers held a general meeting and decided to petition the Social Affairs Bureau today. The various situations are recorded as follows:

Workers' General Meeting: At 3:00 PM yesterday, all the workers held a general meeting at the Rihua branch office in Pudong. First, the chairman reported on the process, and then they began to discuss. It is heard that they resolved (1) to hold a major petition to the Social Affairs Bureau at 10:00 AM on the 29th, (2) to demand that the Japanese be strictly ordered not to refuse workers to resume work, (3) otherwise, according to the factory closure method, each person will receive six months' severance pay, (4) to severely punish worker accomplices, (5) to oppose increasing work and reducing wages, (6) to welcome the released workers back to the workshop.

Japanese Plan: The two arrested female workers, Lu Xiaomei and Ni Jinxiu, were released from the local court. Yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, all the workers welcomed them back to the workshop and set off firecrackers along the way to celebrate. The Municipal Public Security Bureau's Third District Headquarters was notified by the labor union in advance. Since the Japanese refused to allow workers to resume work, they instigated worker accomplices yesterday and recruited new workers to prepare for work. However, all the workers, in view of the Japanese atrocities, were unwilling to break the strike discipline, so no one went.

British Public Bus Company May Resume Work Unconditionally Today

Armed Protection Yesterday to Force Operations

Ticket Seller No. 1's Court Trial Opened Yesterday

Workers Held a Meeting Last Night to Discuss the Approach

After all the ticket sellers of the British Public Bus Company went on strike, the company was protected by armed detectives yesterday and forced to operate Routes 1 and 9. Workers sent representatives to negotiate. It is heard that it has been decided to resume work unconditionally today. The various situations are recorded as follows:

Protected Traffic: In order to maintain traffic, the company was protected by armed detectives sent by the police station yesterday. They forced to operate 14 buses on Route 1 from Jing'an Temple to Laobaizi, 20 A special express buses on Route 9 from Jing'an Temple to Tilanqiao, three B buses, and two C buses. Ticket inspection, writing, and Western plainclothes inspectors served as ticket sellers. They entered the factory early at 10:00 PM and fortunately no conflicts occurred.

General Meeting: All the striking ticket sellers held a workers' general meeting yesterday morning. First, the chairman reported on the process, and then they began to discuss countermeasures against the company. It is heard that they resolved (1) to send six representatives, Nos. 2, 6, 15, 152, 226, and 235, to negotiate directly with the manager of the company, (2) to declare that ticket seller No. 1 is very loyal and to demand that the company bail him out and restore his position, (3) if the above measures are achieved, all the workers will resume work immediately.

Self-Negotiation: Yesterday morning at 3:00 AM, the six representatives elected by all the ticket sellers went to the company on Connaught Road to negotiate with the manager. The manager initially stated that he would terminate the employment contract in accordance with the announcement on the 26th. After negotiation, he agreed to resume work unconditionally. Seeing that the company's attitude was tough, the representatives verbally agreed to resume work unconditionally tomorrow (i.e., this morning).

Court Hearing: Ticket seller No. 1, Zhang Yun, was arrested by the Gordon Road Police Station and taken to the Simple Court of the First Special District Local Court yesterday. Judge Shen Shumu questioned him. First, the police lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated that the defendant incited all the ticket sellers to strike on the morning of the 25th and prosecuted him for obstructing freedom in accordance with Article 318 of the Criminal Code. Zhang Yun absolutely denied it. Judge Shen then ordered a continuation of the hearing at a later date.

Company Treatment: Ticket sellers told a reporter from Xinsheng News Agency that the company's treatment has always been oppressive. In the past, old ticket sellers went on strike because they could not bear the oppression, and as a result, they were completely unemployed. This time, we are helping ticket seller No. 1, and the company is imitating the previous method of dismissing all of us. During our service, if we are found to be skimming money from ticket sales, we will be immediately dismissed and punished according to the criminal law. Therefore, all the ticket sellers do not skim money, but the company still slanders the workers. As for the copper coins for ticket sales, the company stipulates 70,000 coins for Route 1, 75,000 coins for Route 2, 73,000 coins for Route 5, 45,000 coins for Routes 6 and 7, 97,000 coins for Route 9, and 88,000 coins for Route 10. If the above regulations are exceeded, they will be rewarded with 40 cents, and 20 cents for driving the bus.

Resume Work Today: After the six representatives negotiated with the manager of the company, they immediately convened a general meeting to report on the negotiation process and discuss solutions. It is heard that two-thirds of the ticket sellers advocated resuming work unconditionally and at the same time trying to bail out the other one-third ticket sellers. They advocated continuing the strike and vowing not to resume work until the goal is achieved. It is heard that the result is to resume work this morning, but it is still unpredictable whether there will be changes before the resumption of work.

Joint Meeting of District Secretaries of the Pharmaceutical Industry Held Yesterday

Officially Established the Reorganization Committee

And Exercises All Powers

The Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union has been declining due to the incompetence of the two responsible persons, so the workers in the industry have voluntarily organized a reorganization committee and taken over the labor union. However, because the internal organization of the reorganization committee has not been sound, many workers have recently advocated that the reorganization committee needs to be reorganized. In order to accept the will of the masses, the reorganization committee convened a joint meeting of district secretaries at 1:00 PM yesterday. More than 100 secretaries from South Shanghai District, West Shanghai District, French Concession District, Central Shanghai District, American Concession District, Xinzha District, Zhabei District, Pudong District, Wusong District, etc. attended. Fang Qingjian was elected chairman, and Feng Xingkang was the recorder. The meeting proceeded in due form. First, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, and the secretaries expressed their opinions (omitted). Then, Fang Zheng, Huang Zhisan, Kong Baogen, Hua Qiang, Yi Guifang, Ye Dingzhong, Fang Qingjian, Fang Qinghe, Feng Xingkang, Chen Hezhi, Ye Baozhong, Huang Youxiang, Mu Fusheng, Chen Zancheng, Zhao Xian'an, Wang Kaichun, Ye Xingshou, Lu Zhixiang, Chen Fu, Xu Chubao, Zhao Zhenhui, and other 21 people were elected as reorganization committee members to establish the Shanghai Municipal Pharmaceutical Workers' Nine District Joint Reorganization Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union Committee. Next, the following proposals were passed: (1) This association exercises its powers. From today, it exercises all its powers. If there are labor-capital disputes or labor disputes, this association will be responsible for handling them. Passed. (2) Stop the activities of the Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union. Since the Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union has been taken over by our workers and is undergoing reorganization, this name can no longer exist, and no one may use this name to carry out activities outside. Passed. (3) The former reorganization committee should handle the handover. The reorganization of the labor union is now the responsibility of this association, and the former reorganization committee should hand over all procedures to this association for handling. Passed. (4) This case of workers joining the industry association. All pharmaceutical workers, whether internal or external, are skilled workers and physical laborers, and there is no reason to join the industry association. Moreover, now that the Central Committee is submitting amendments to the Labor Law and the Factory Law to the First Plenary Session, if the industry association forces them to join, our workers will oppose it to the death. Passed. (5) Employers will dismiss workers by taking advantage of the New Year. Send a letter to warn the industry association that employers must not dismiss workers by taking advantage of the New Year. If any workers are dismissed, they can report to this association immediately, and we will argue reasonably to ensure the safety of their jobs. Passed. (6) Implement the wage increase resolution passed by the previous general membership meeting. The wage increase issue is currently an urgent request of our workers. A resolution was passed at the previous general membership meeting, but it has not yet been implemented. It should be submitted to the employers for request as soon as possible. Passed.

Petition from Two Postal Unions to Abolish the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau

Support Postal Services with Postal Economics

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Postal Employees' Union, in a submission to the Fourth Plenary Session of the First Central Committee, appealed to abolish the separately established Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau, to return its functions to the Postal Administration, and to stipulate that postal economics be exclusively used to expand postal services, maintain the postal foundation, and seek postal line development. It is noted that on March 15th of last year, the Ministry of Transportation suddenly divided the postal savings and remittance business, establishing a separate Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau directly under the Ministry of Transportation, standing alongside the Postal Administration. Since the establishment of this bureau, it has disrupted the postal system and undermined postal institutions. While the disadvantages may seem small, the impact on postal economic income and the waste of national public funds are significant. The savings and remittance business is inseparable from postal services; anyone working in the postal service or familiar with its internal operations knows this. Therefore, at the outset of the bureau's separation, the unions repeatedly cried out to salvage the situation, and repeatedly offered modest proposals to the government. Unfortunately, their humble concerns were obscured by the selfish motives of a few, failing to achieve what the unions hoped for. Their sincere loyalty remains a matter of regret to this day. However, it was still hoped that after the establishment of the General Bureau, it would uphold fairness and impartiality, and avoid plunging China's postal service, established for over thirty years, into an irrecoverable state, while providing opportunities for those who sought to profit from it. Unexpectedly, the situation deteriorated and grew worse. Since the establishment of the General Bureau, it has employed non-experts, engaged in secretive administration, created unrealistic plans, and spent lavishly. Previously, when the Postal Administration managed the business, it felt like it was steadily improving and saving twice as much in expenses. With further improvements, it would have made even greater progress. But now, it lacks vitality. Furthermore, after being divided by the General Bureau, the Postal Administration, though nominally coexisting, had its personnel, administration, economy, and various other aspects restricted. This greatly hinders the future of the postal service. Looking back at the historical facts of the past year, one cannot help but feel deeply saddened. The Postal Administration has managed the savings and remittance business for over thirty years, adhering to a strict policy and imposing appropriate restrictions on savings, yet deposits still reached over ten million yuan. The remittance business was managed effectively, with significant progress made. Because it was under the jurisdiction of the Postal Administration itself, operations were extremely convenient, there was no redundant personnel, and the organization was consistent and well-organized. Currently, while savings have also increased under the General Bureau, this increase is due to the elimination of the previous strict policies and the removal of restrictions on deposits. Therefore, while it may appear to be developing on the surface, it is actually a natural phenomenon. As for the remittance business, it is also an annual improvement that is to be expected. Regardless of whether it is managed by the Postal Administration or the General Bureau, the expected progress cannot be said to have only occurred after the division. In short, if one wants to improve the savings and remittance business, one can improve it based on its original state. Why must it be divided and split before speaking of improvement? This is truly because those who masterminded it harbored ulterior motives from the beginning of the division. The evidence is clear. Based on facts and theories, the postal savings and remittance business must be returned to the Postal Administration to save the postal service from its dangerous path and prevent it from being destroyed and declining to the point of collapse. This is the first point. China has been plagued by years of internal warfare, and the people's livelihood has been depleted. The fact that the postal service has been able to struggle to survive and maintain its achievements of over thirty years without collapsing is due to the use of postal economics to maintain postal operations. However, compared to the achievements of European and American countries, it still lags far behind. Therefore, China's postal service urgently needs to be expanded, and shortened postal lines must be restored immediately. The existing bureaus should be expanded, new inland post offices should be established, and postal routes should be extended. All of these things, within the scope of what postal economics can afford, are urgent and essential plans. After China's production [unclear], any construction that is not in line with national conditions and the people's livelihood can be implemented slowly, to seek what suits the needs of our people. As is the case with our postal service, it must be expanded as much as possible.

Page 10

Therefore, at this time, if postal economics have surplus resources, they should be used for postal services first. Postal transportation will then be convenient, and the national economy and the people's livelihood will benefit. Otherwise, if the financial resources of the postal service are used to try out national embellishments such as the so-called aviation business, the postal service will lose millions, and in reality, it will not benefit the national economy and the people's livelihood. On the contrary, the postal service that the people rely on for transportation will not be actively expanded. This is what the unions are very concerned about and cannot help but consider a bad plan. In short, the aviation business may also be something that the country should undertake, but the priorities must be distinguished. In China today, are postal services or aviation more important? Which is more needed by the people? Even if the aviation business is twice as important as postal services, the government should raise large sums of money separately to establish it with all its might, so as not to hinder the foundation of other state-run enterprises and impede their future development. Otherwise, the aviation business will not be successful, and the great postal service will be implicated and even overturned. This is why the unions are sincerely concerned and cannot help but speak out, not daring to oppose the aviation business, but specifically wanting to maintain the postal service and develop its future to meet the needs of the people. Therefore, the unions believe that postal economics should be used for postal services first and should not be allocated to other purposes, so as to benefit the people's needs. This is the second point. In summary, what has been said is out of love for the postal service and to consolidate its foundation. The members of the unions serve the postal service and rely on it for their livelihood. What they have presented is based on sincerity. They respectfully hope that the conference will open, that national unity and peace will be seen again, and that all matters will be rectified. They dare to present these verbose words, appealing to the conference to quickly review and approve them, and to implement them. Not only will the future of the postal service be fortunate, but the people of the whole country will benefit from it. The presentation is urgent, and they cannot wait to receive instructions. They respectfully present this to the Fourth Plenary Session of the First Central Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang.

Overseas Chinese Continue to Return to China

Since sending ships to Yokohama to transport a batch of overseas Chinese who were unable to return to China, there are still over 2,000 overseas Chinese in various parts of Japan who cannot return. From December 1st to yesterday, Zheng Shoujin, Lin Youxiang, Qian Jinmin, and 485 others arrived in Shanghai successively by ship from Kobe, Moji, Nagasaki, and other places. Most of those returning this time are from Fujian. It is said that there are over a thousand overseas Chinese living in Japan with no means of support, urgently awaiting the government to find a way to transport them back, otherwise they will be stranded in a foreign land.

Chinese Ships Suspend Sailings on Northern Routes

Affected by Violent Japanese Military Actions

Both Freight and Passengers Decrease

Japanese Troops March into Tianjin: In recent days, various Shanghai merchant guilds have received telegrams from Tianjin stating that over 2,000 Japanese troops have marched into Tianjin from Tanggu. In the direction of Lushun, Japanese warships have also sailed to Tianjin and Dagukou, advancing by land and sea. The Chinese in Tianjin, mindful of the previous disturbances caused by Japanese troops, are increasingly panicked by the entry of violent Japanese troops into the concession.

Stagnation of Commercial Goods Transportation: Tianjin merchants have recently suspended cargo transportation due to the tense situation in North China. However, as it is also the end of the year, more flour is being transported. Eight to ninety thousand bags were shipped in the past two days. The transportation of other goods has plummeted. There is also a shortage of passengers traveling from Shanghai to Tianjin, resulting in losses for all outbound voyages on Northern routes.

Chinese Ships Suspend Sailings Between Shanghai and Tianjin: The Shanghai-Tianjin route is normally served by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's regular ships, Xin Feng and Xin Ming. Recently, affected by Japanese military actions, business has declined. Northern ports have also frozen and closed due to ice. Therefore, the company decided to suspend the Northern routes and wait for the situation to stabilize before resuming operations. The company has reassigned Xin Feng to the South China route, sailing to Shantou, Xiamen, and other ports, and Xin Ming has been reassigned to the Yangtze River, carrying American wheat from Shanghai to Wuhu, Hankou, and other ports for unloading.

The Maritime Quarantine Service Declares Xiamen an Epidemic Port for Smallpox

The Maritime Quarantine Service received a telegram from the Xiamen Maritime Quarantine Station, stating that smallpox is very prevalent in Xiamen. Statistics show that dozens of people are dying from smallpox every day. Xiamen has been officially declared an epidemic port. At the same time, a telegram was received from Shantou regarding the same situation. Based on these reports, notices were sent to all seaports in China and abroad, confirming Xiamen as an epidemic port. A public announcement was also published, stating that all ships sailing from Xiamen or transiting through Xiamen must first anchor at Wusongkou and await inspection by medical officers before entering the port.

Results of the Anti-Drug Essay Competition for Middle Schools Announced

First Place: Yu Yusheng from Zhenjiang Middle School

The results of the 3rd Anti-Drug Essay Competition for Middle School Students have been announced. The Education Department of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association previously announced the names of the students selected in the preliminary round, as well as the winners in the university group. Ma Cunkun from Central University won first place in the university group and, in addition to receiving a medal and certificate, was awarded a cash prize of one hundred yuan, which was also remitted yesterday. It has been reported that the evaluation of the middle school group was delayed due to the busy schedules of the judges. The scores were finally reviewed and determined yesterday, and the six winners were selected. First place went to Yu Yusheng from Zhenjiang Middle School, for his essay titled "The Impact of Opium Monopoly on the Nation and the People's Livelihood." Second place went to Wang Chaoqun from Hunan Provincial Third Middle School, for his essay titled "What Young Students Should Know in the Anti-Drug Movement." Third place went to Cao Yinliang from Yangzhou Middle School. Fourth place went to Xu Dawen from Jiangxi Second Vocational School. Fifth place went to Jin Juewen from Hangzhou Zongwen Middle School. The titles of their essays were all "Opium Monopoly Violates Sun Yat-sen's Anti-Drug Teachings." Sixth place went to Zhu Qize from Zhejiang Provincial High School, for his essay titled "The Significance and Value of China's Anti-Drug Movement." There are three alternate winners: (1) Wang Weiyi from Shanghai City North Middle School, (2) Su Jintang from Shandong Provincial Ninth Middle School, (3) Ji Tongwen from Wuxi Middle School. The six winners will each receive a gold and silver medal and a certificate. Yu Yusheng from Zhenjiang Middle School, who won first place, will also receive a cash prize of fifty yuan as an encouragement. The three alternate winners will each receive a certificate and several anti-drug books. All other students who participated in the competition, over a hundred in total, will each receive a year's subscription to the Anti-Drug Monthly as a souvenir.

Lawyer's Association Declaration

The Shanghai Lawyers' Association's declaration states: In the past, the authorities, using the name of the Kuomintang, adhered to the Kuomintang's political program to govern the country. Over the past five years, the realization of the Kuomintang's political program in society has been less than one in a hundred. What society has endured are war disasters, banditry, poverty, corruption, and the collapse of all governance, compounded by unprecedented natural disasters and the invasion of powerful enemies. The public's attitude toward the authorities has shifted from suspicion to disappointment, and from disappointment to resentment. Now, the entire country is in turmoil and cannot continue like this. The previous Shanghai Peace Conference resolved to reform party affairs and the political system. Former Chairman Chiang has already resigned. The Fourth Plenary Session of the First Central Committee is born of the moment. Organizational changes in the central region are imperative. However, the succeeding authorities, taking office amidst crises, will face difficulties a hundredfold greater than usual. We, as members of this association, mindful of the admonition against overstepping our bounds, and concerned about national governance, do not wish to comment excessively. However, in a leaking boat amidst wind and rain, when beams are broken and rafters collapse, even the silent golden statue cannot escape unscathed. Therefore, based on the principle of shared responsibility, and considering the deepest pains felt by the public, we summarize fourteen issues: Years of civil war, the people unable to bear it, first. Lack of civil rights, the public's opinions unable to be expressed, second. Loss of territory, the nation's sovereignty fragmented, third. Poor diplomacy, isolated and without assistance, fourth. Unreformed military system, neglected national defense, fifth. Disordered finances, unclear income and expenditure, sixth. Class struggle, lacking means of resolution, seventh. Frequent disasters, no effective relief, eighth. Furthermore, the lack of education, backward production, failed justice, corrupt officials, obstructed transportation, and unsuccessful resettlement are all detrimental to the nation and the people. Whenever the people think of these things, some gnash their teeth in anger, while others hang their heads in despair, and they uniformly attribute these to the shortcomings of the authorities. If the succeeding authorities cannot establish a plan in advance, clearly demonstrate it to the people, abandon deception, and establish great trust, then the future of the country will not be easy to predict. We summarize these fourteen points and ask the succeeding authorities to declare their policy. Some may suspect this is just the same old story, unrelated to the grand scheme. We dare to elaborate on its relevance for discussion with people across the country, which will surely be of benefit. The prominent forces within the country can be grouped into four: Nanjing, Guangdong, Shanxi, and Fengtian (Liaoning). Yunnan, Guizhou, Sichuan, Hunan, and the latent Red Party are not included. The previous authorities, shouting the slogan of unification, spared no effort to overcome all difficulties to achieve it. The result was the same failure as previous warlords. The opposition forces remain divided, and their infighting and plotting increase daily. The continuous civil war has depleted the nation's strength and destroyed talent, leaving the public unable to live in peace, and stifling all vitality. When faced with the invasion of a powerful neighbor, each force looks at each other in astonishment, daring not to act. All living beings feel extreme heartache. How should we select and implement reforms, and choose stable strategies to balance the various forces, bring all interests into alignment, so as to permanently end civil war and stabilize the people's livelihood? This is what those who plan for the country should consider first. The national title is Republic, the party title is Kuomintang, but the public is not allowed to interfere in any government affairs. Since the authorities' words and actions contradict each other, the people are naturally alienated. The saying "the people can carry the boat, but they can also capsize it" should be deeply considered. Moreover, the national crisis is urgent, and future troubles are looming. A single tree is hard to support, but many hands make light work. How should we implement constitutionalism and promote democracy, so that the entire nation can work together to bear the burden of difficulties? This is what those who plan for the country should consider first. The eastern provinces, with vast fertile lands and inexhaustible resources, are the source of sustenance for the entire nation, and the lifeblood of future generations. Domestic public opinion for war is willing to sacrifice lives for it, not just to maintain face and protect national rights. Moreover, if the balance of power is not maintained, the disaster of dismemberment will inevitably occur. If we do not drive out the invading bandits, then the country, however large, will not be enough to satisfy the greedy appetite of the imperialists. How should we recover lost territories and complete the national territory? This is the first step in stabilizing the people's hearts and supporting the nation's destiny. In the past, the authorities, on one hand, sought to eliminate the communists and sever relations with Russia, and on the other hand, supported party affairs and advocated revolutionary diplomacy. Furthermore, because of their focus on civil war, they neglected foreign affairs, resulting in a large number of vacant international diplomatic posts, leading to isolation in the international community. If not for the constraints of international treaties such as the League of Nations Covenant, the Nine-Power Treaty, and the Kellogg-Briand Pact, the cold and cruel face of the international community would be unbearable for us to face. How should we determine our diplomatic policy to enhance our international standing? This is also a crucial way to secure domestic peace, resist foreign aggression, and consolidate the foundation of the nation. Recruiting soldiers can easily lead to warlordism. In recent years, the concepts of "cherishing strength" and "maintaining territory" have filled the minds of soldiers, fostering a bad habit of being brave in internal conflicts and cowardly in resisting foreign invasion. The nation's annual revenue is mostly used to support the military, yet when invaders and bandits suddenly arrive, it is as if they are entering an uninhabited land. All the nation's sea and air fortresses are insufficient to defend themselves, and weapons and ammunition are even more insufficient to supply themselves. Alas, the people have nowhere to die! How should we strengthen national defense and reform the military system? This is an urgent task for establishing the nation. Finance is the lifeblood of the nation. Every bit of it comes from the people. In the past, the authorities took every penny and used it like dirt. It is said that to facilitate civil war, many telegraph operators were paid monthly salaries of over ten thousand yuan. The cost of buying a confidential telegram was tens of thousands without compunction. Some large armies were purchasing equipment at exorbitant prices. There was no limit. In recent years, the excessive issuance of public bonds and the improper collection of revenue have all been driven by inflated expenditures and abuse. Public grievances are boiling, and national credibility has been swept away. Can this be allowed to continue? How should we thoroughly reorganize and conduct public audits, showing the people how funds are used, and demonstrating great trust to both domestic and foreign entities? This is the foundation for maintaining the people's hearts. Class struggle is the result of unequal living conditions and a prelude to social collapse. At the end of the nineteenth century, German economists and politicians were uniquely insightful enough to see this trend and created systems such as labor insurance and employment services to appease workers (which have now become extensive international legislation). This was able to stabilize society, even after experiencing the Great War and great revolution and enduring all the painful hardships humans can suffer, without shaking the social structure. Recently, mechanical progress has been rapid, eliminating the need for human muscle labor. However, the German authorities, still based on their traditional political beliefs, restricted factories from using new machinery to prevent unemployment. This historical fact is a powerful guide for stabilizing society. Our authorities verbally promote agricultural and industrial policies, but the suffering of farmers and workers has only increased. International best practices such as labor insurance have never been mentioned, while on the other hand, they engage in high-pressure suppression and talk of eliminating communists, which is like climbing a tree to catch a fish or heading south by driving the chariot north. How should we protect the interests of workers to quell class struggle and stabilize the lives of the people? This is an essential component for pacifying the nation. Our country is based on agriculture, with over 85% of the population being farmers. However, political orders are not well-executed, internal strife does not cease, and international economic aggression increases daily. Even in years of good harvests, it is difficult to achieve self-sufficiency for every family. In the event of floods or droughts, the government has no grain reserves, and individuals have no food for the next day. Although charitable organizations can provide some relief, it is often like using a cart of water to put out a cart of burning firewood, unable to alleviate hunger and cold. The young and strong scatter in all directions, while the old and weak are left in ditches. According to historical accounts, powerful individuals have often hijacked disaster victims, leading to widespread turmoil and the overthrow of political power. This year, there are tens of millions of disaster victims in fourteen provinces. The bitter cold is only halfway through, and many spring crops have not yet been planted. The dangerous future is just beginning. How should we comfort the afflicted and save the dying? How should we prevent disasters and prepare for the future? These are the foundations for stabilizing society. Education is essential for developing the natural talents of the people. Modern nations implement compulsory education to strive for universal access. This has not been seen in our country. Illiteracy is rampant, and out-of-school children are all over the country, especially in regions afflicted by war and disaster. The educational methods adopted in the past were mostly insincere, incomplete, and impractical, running counter to the idea of universal compulsory education. If this continues, not only will the nation's natural talents never develop, but national consciousness will become increasingly numb, class divisions will deepen, and the spirit of struggle will become more acute. This is a major hidden worry for the future. How should we determine an educational plan to place the entire nation on the same level and progress alongside other nations in the world? This is essential for supporting the survival of the nation and cultivating the foundation of the country. Developing production is essential for improving the people's livelihoods. Our country's material resources are extremely abundant, but land lies barren and goods are abandoned, leaving the general public in hunger and cold, unable to make a living. The reason for this is simply the lack of skills and the inability to develop resources, and the lack of laws to guarantee the credibility of production. As a result, those who handle affairs are always at a loss, and those with capital hesitate to invest. How should we recruit talent and attract capital to develop production and improve livelihoods? This is the most important task for those who lead the country. The judicial organs represent the nation in maintaining the law. Life and freedom depend on their protection, and rights and obligations are balanced through them. Since our country's reforms, we have inherited the European legal system by blindly copying it, resulting in a system that is ill-fitting. Moreover, due to constant changes, there are many gaps and flaws. Since the national government established its capital in Nanjing, the judicial organization has not made any progress. Instead, special trials and administrative penalties have fragmented the authority of the courts and disrupted the judicial system. On the one hand, court funding has been decreasing, and judicial talent has been scattered and withered. As a result, the people view law officials as venomous snakes and the courts as ghost dens. The law has lost its credibility, and the people have no standards to follow. How should we thoroughly reorganize this so that legal professionals can fulfill their duties, and the people can have norms to follow? This is an urgent task. When the national government was first established, the officials employed were not always based on qualifications and grades. As political tides rose and fell, subordinate officials often followed senior officials. Those who sought official positions would not hesitate to curry favor with influential figures and bribe their way into power. Those who gained positions often felt like they were only in office for a short time, seeking only immediate gains and neglecting long-term planning. The corruption of the officialdom has infected the entire country. The alienation of the people is mainly due to this. How should we rectify the official system and clarify the governance of officials? This is also an essential way to maintain the people's hearts. The transportation system of a nation is like the circulatory system of a person. Obstruction of transportation is like paralysis, causing the loss of basic functions. Our country's transportation is hindered, preventing progress in military, political, cultural, and commercial fields. Even the wisest will sigh in despair. How should we strive to improve this? This is the basis for initiating all administrative affairs. Although our country has a large population, the border areas have vast and uninhabited lands. Since the abolition of military settlements at the end of the Qing Dynasty, resettlement has long been discontinued. Like ivory that invites its own destruction, hoarding only invites theft. Since we abandon vast fields, it is inevitable that powerful neighbors will covet them. How should we facilitate resettlement and strengthen the border areas? This is also of great concern to the national economy and the people's livelihood. All these fourteen issues are what the people urgently demand but have not been able to get answers to from the previous authorities. Since the succeeding leaders are not satisfied with the current situation, they should consider these major issues thoroughly. It is hoped that they will issue a great call, shaking and awakening the masses, so that the people can all benefit. Furthermore, those who observe the country are often shocked by the politics of the newly established Soviet Russia. The key to their success, unmatched by other nations, lies in two things: (1) Before the promulgation of any policy, it must be carefully considered by a design agency that brings together numerous experts, ensuring that it is appropriate before being implemented; (2) A large-scale supervisory agency is established, granting it broad powers. From the government to the people, all organizations are under its watchful eyes and strict supervision. Anyone who does not act according to the planned plans or national laws is immediately subject to severe and effective measures. This ensures that there is no backlog of paperwork and that orders are carried out. Our country's officials are accustomed to following old practices. Policies and reality often do not align. Shang Yang said, "All countries have laws, but they lack a method to ensure that laws are enforced." We hope that in the future, when the authorities are designing and planning, they will gather input from various sources, and not simply rely on high-ranking officials to draft policies based on their own opinions. After the promulgation, they must also conduct thorough supervision to ensure that it is implemented, and not just rely on empty words, repeating the mistake of attempting everything and accomplishing nothing. Gentlemen of the country, do not take these words lightly.

Footprints on Lime Powder

A Theft Case of Over 6,000 Yuan Solved

Servant Steals Due to Lack of Funds for Wedding

Hu Shouyao, a resident of No. 282 Aiwenyi Road, runs a yarn business and is considered a well-to-do family. Recently, due to his mother's death, he needed a large sum of money, so he kept 7,000 yuan in banknotes and silver coins in the drawer of his accounting room's desk. Unexpectedly, in the middle of the night on the 25th of this month, a thief broke into the room and stole the money. The next morning, upon discovery, it was found that 6,548 yuan and three jiao had been stolen. The glass window of the accounting room was also broken. The case was reported to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. They found that a bucket of lime powder in the room appeared to have been kicked over by the thief. As a result, there was lime powder scattered on the floor, and the thief, inadvertently, stepped in the powder, leaving behind shoe prints. However, after thoroughly inspecting the traces, they did not extend outside the house, so it was determined that the theft was committed by someone inside the house. Therefore, all male and female servants in the Hu family were questioned one by one. Soon, it was discovered that the soles of the shoes of a servant named Xu Jinhong also had lime powder on them. His shoes were taken and compared with the shoe prints on the floor, and they matched perfectly. Thus, the case was solved. Upon further investigation, Xu, realizing that it was difficult to deny the accusations, confessed everything. He said that he was planning to get married but lacked the financial means. Last night, he saw that the master had placed a large amount of money in the drawer, and the key was on the table. He was blinded by greed and broke into the room to steal the money. The stolen silver coins were hidden in the stove in the kitchen, and the banknotes were placed in the pillowcase, without having spent a single cent. The detectives searched as he said and found the original stolen goods, without any missing. Xu was taken to the police station and detained. Xu is only 21 years old and has worked for the Hu family for eight years without any previous misconduct. His parents and grandmother are still in his hometown. After he was arrested, his father heard the news and came to Shanghai to appeal. Yesterday morning, the police escorted Xu to the First Special District Local Court, where he was interrogated by Judge Wu Tingqi. Xu still pleaded guilty and said that he had acted out of a momentary mistake. He begged for forgiveness and promised never to do it again. His master, Hu Shouyao, was also very generous and sent his bookkeeper, Zheng Zhongren, to the court to represent him, requesting that the judge consider the defendant's first-time offense and give him a lenient sentence. Judge Wu sentenced the defendant, Xu Jinhong, to six months of imprisonment for the crime of theft, suspended for three years. During the probation period, his family members were responsible for supervising his conduct. The stolen goods were returned to the plaintiff.

Reactions to the Ferry Fare Increase

The Pudong Fellow-Provincials Association received a letter from members Xu Zuoxun and others regarding the increase in ferry fares in Pudong, requesting that they submit it to the Municipal Government to rescind the order. The letter stated: Respectfully, on the 18th of this month, Zuoxun and others saw a report stating that the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, considering that the ticket prices of various ferry terminals and the distance of the routes did not match the current traffic conditions, submitted a request to the Municipal Government to adjust the fares accordingly. This measure is scheduled to take effect on January 1 of next year. The second-class fare from Shanghai to Donggou, originally one jiao, will be increased by two fen, based on the actual measurement of the waterway by the Junpu Bureau, which is 34,000 feet. The second-class fare from Donggou to Gaoqiao, originally five fen, which is 16,000 feet, less than half the distance from Shanghai to Donggou, will be increased by three fen, even though it is a remote area. On the west side, before the terminals are improved, the second-class fare from Shanghai to Xidu, originally five fen, which is 25,000 feet, will be increased by two fen. The second-class fare from Xidu to Donggou, originally five fen, which is 14,000 feet, will also be increased by two fen. According to the fares set above, there is actually an increase without any decrease. Zuoxun and others further checked the business report of the Public Utilities Bureau and found that the revenue of the Municipal Ferry in the second half of the 19th year (1930) had increased compared to the previous period. The total ticket revenue for the 19th year was 108,139 yuan, 5 jiao, and 3 fen. The operating expenses were 89,687 yuan, 7 jiao, and 7 fen. After offsetting the revenue and expenses, there was a surplus of 88,451 yuan, 7 jiao, and 6 fen, so there is no need to increase the ferry fares. Moreover, the Municipal Ferry is one of the public utilities, and it is of great importance to facilitate public transportation, which cannot be compared to businesses seeking profits. During this time of national crisis, all industries are in decline, and commerce and industry are stagnant. In addition, this year's agricultural production in Pudong has been poor, and the livelihood of ordinary people is already extremely difficult. Now, the increase in ferry fares is truly unaffordable. We have always admired your association for seeking welfare for fellow villagers, so we have described the situation in detail and hope that you will review it and submit it to the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Public Utilities Bureau for approval to rescind the order and avoid increasing ferry fares, so as to comply with the public's feelings and relieve the people's distress. This is truly a matter of public benefit.

Interception of the Jiangxi Finance Bureau Chief Who Fled to Shanghai with Embezzled Funds

Ordered to be Sent to the Provincial Government for Verification

Fu Gengtang, the Chief of the Finance Bureau of Linchuan County, Jiangxi Province, collected all the funds from the bureau on the 18th of this month, claiming to be sending them to the Finance Department in the provincial capital. However, he was suddenly robbed by bandits en route, and all the cash was lost. Only a remittance slip for 4,000 yuan, which had been exchanged at Shengchang Trust and Savings Bank at No. 238 Dean Lane, North Suzhou Road, Shanghai, remained. Fu then took this remittance slip and traveled to Shanghai by a roundabout route, without first reporting to the Finance Department. The provincial government waited until the 22nd of this month and learned that Fu had arrived in Shanghai. They then telegraphed the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, requesting investigation and arrest for embezzlement and escape, and to prevent the withdrawal of funds. Deputy Director Yu dispatched Xie Yuzeng, a staff member from the custody and release section, and detective Shan Bin, to the Huizhaishi Police Station, and additional Chinese and foreign detectives were dispatched to Shengchang Trust and Savings Bank to investigate. Fu had not yet arrived in Shanghai. It was not until noon on the 24th of this month that Fu arrived in Shanghai and went to the bank to withdraw the funds. He was immediately detained and taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Local Court, where he was interrogated by Judge Wu Tingqi. Wang Yaotang, the translator of the police station, explained the situation and presented the remittance slip found on Fu Gengtang as evidence. Fu Gengtang denied embezzling and escaping, claiming that he was sending the funds to the province when he was illegally inspected by unmarked armed forces who stole the cash. That is why he came to Shanghai to exchange the remittance slip. He also claimed to have reported the situation to his superiors. Judge Wu ruled that since the Jiangxi Provincial Government had already sent a telegram requesting extradition, the defendant could file a complaint with the provincial government regarding whether he had embezzled and escaped, which was not for this court to investigate. Therefore, Fu Gengtang, along with the remittance slip, was handed over to the officers from the Municipal Police Bureau and escorted back to Jiangxi Province for investigation.

Henan County Magistrate Allowed to be Extradited

Jin Yuzhen, the former Magistrate of Xinzheng County, Henan Province, left his post in June of this year without waiting for the handover and entrusted You Lunwu, the Chief of the First Section, to handle the handover on his behalf. Later, it was discovered that there was a shortage of more than 1,300 yuan in public funds. Jin could not be found, and You was detained and given a deadline to repay the funds. However, Jin was hiding in Shanghai. You Lunwu has been detained for six months now. After You reported to the Finance Department, an arrest warrant was issued. Now, You's son, Suquan, came to Shanghai and learned that Jin was hiding at No. 13 Peipin Lane, Huanghe Road, in the French Concession. He immediately reported this to the Municipal Police Bureau, which sent a letter to the Second Special District Court to issue an arrest warrant. The police were dispatched to arrest Jin and escort him to the Second Special District Court for questioning. He was ordered to wait for the Municipal Police Bureau to send personnel to extradite him back for trial. This has been reported in the previous news. Yesterday, the Municipal Police Bureau sent personnel to the Second Special District Court for extradition. Judge Luo presided over the Criminal Division and ordered the defendant to be brought to court for questioning. Jin protested loudly, saying that he should not be detained based on a single piece of paper and requested the court to guarantee his freedom. The official replied that if he had a reason, he should go to Henan to appeal. Therefore, the defendant was allowed to be taken away by the personnel from the Municipal Police Bureau and escorted back for trial.

Fireworks Explosion Injures People

Kuai Li, who runs a fireworks business at No. 200 Caopeng, Yutong Road, Zhabei, accidentally dropped a firework on the ground while transporting it yesterday morning around 10:00 a.m., causing it to explode and catch fire. The fire brigade was dispatched to the scene to extinguish the fire, and no major disaster occurred. However, Xia Zhang, a woman from Yancheng, and Shi Zhaorong and Ni Lirong from Funing were burned on their heads, faces, waists, and hands. The police arrested Kuai Li and Jiang Xu, who lived with him, and took them to the Second Division of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau for questioning.

Russian Jealousy and Murder of a Dancer

A Russian man named Komi Zhukov, working in a bar on Broadway, was in love with a woman named Bai Zhiwei, a dancer at a dance hall in the French Concession. Their relationship was initially very good and they were very close. However, the woman recently became romantically involved with another man, causing Komi Zhukov to become jealous. He broke into her residence at 20 Huishan Road last night and stabbed her in the throat several times with a fruit knife, severing half of her trachea. She fell to the ground and died instantly. Komi Zhukov did not try to escape after the murder. The Huishan police station was notified, arrested Komi, and will bring him to court for trial.

Murder of Wife in a Moment of Anger

The Murderer Sent to Court for Review

The woman, Zhu Da Shi, was 28 years old, from Danyang, and lived at house number 70, Sande Lane, Meibaige Road. Her husband, Zhu Genfa, 24 years old, worked as a worker in a printing house. The couple had been married for six years. Genfa had been experiencing unusual economic hardship recently, and creditors were constantly demanding payment, which made him very distressed. On the morning of the 25th of this month, the couple argued over a trivial matter. In a fit of anger, Genfa stabbed his wife, Zhu Da Shi, in the throat twice with a small knife he was carrying. Da Shi was severely injured, fainted, and bled profusely. Wang Zhihai discovered the incident and reported it to the Xinzha police station, which dispatched detectives to investigate. Da Shi was sent to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but she died soon after. Her body was taken to the forensic examination center on Philan Road. Zhu Genfa was arrested and taken to the police station. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, the prosecutor of the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Wei Ligong and clerk Liu Chun, arrived at the center to examine the body. They took their official positions and interrogated Zhu Genfa, who confessed, "We usually got along very well. At the time, I was really angry and stabbed her in the throat twice with a knife." Wang Zhihai also testified. Guo君 ruled that the deceased, Zhu Da Shi, had indeed died from knife wounds to the throat. The perpetrator, Zhu Genfa, was prosecuted by the police station and should be sent to court for review. A small knife was temporarily stored in the police station, and the body was handed over to Pushan Villa for burial.

Woman Requests Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association to Investigate the Whereabouts of Her Husband, Yu Ailin

Suspect in Liu Jinshan Case

Yu Ailin, a native of Ningbo, is 34 years old and works as an assistant foreman in the coppersmith section of the Shanghai Electric Tramway Company (Hed Road section). On the 15th of this month, he was implicated in the case of his friend, Liu Jinshan, and was arrested by the Jing'an Temple police station and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation. Those arrested at the same time included Liu Jinshan's elder brother, Liu Kuiyuan, and his wife, Tang Xuelan. At that time, Wang Bin, an inspector from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, came to the court to request the transfer of the prisoners, which was approved. Yu Ailin's wife, Yu Tu Shi, believed that her husband was innocent and requested the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association in Shanghai to send a letter to clear his name. Later, the military law office of the Garrison Headquarters replied that the case of Yu Ailin et al. was still at the Special District Court and had not yet been transferred to the headquarters. The association immediately informed Yu Wang Shi. Upon hearing this, she became very anxious. Yu Ailin et al. had been taken away by an inspector from the Garrison Headquarters on the 16th of this month, but it had been several days and they had not yet arrived at the headquarters. She was deeply concerned that there was something hidden and requested the association to find out the truth.

Black and White Photography Society Photography Exhibition

All Proceeds Donated to Flood Relief

The Black and White Photography Society is organized by loyal members of the photography community. Although it has only been established for two years, it has been diligently working on in-depth study and has not rushed to hold public exhibitions. Recently, the society felt that the Chinese people were busy running around to deal with the national crisis and had no time to care for the compatriots in the flood-stricken areas who were suffering from cold and hunger this summer. It gathered photographic works from all its members, selected hundreds of excellent pieces, and borrowed the photography room of the Shishi News Agency in the Xiaohuayuan on Sanma Road for a public exhibition for three days, starting on New Year's Day of the 21st year. All works were priced for sale to donate to the flood-stricken areas. Although the amount is small, it shows the society's intention to save the nation through art, which can be an awakening for the art community. It is expected that art photography enthusiasts will compete to visit and happily purchase the products to support the effort.

Reward Offered for Lost Boy

The Yan family, located at number 24, Gongyi Lane, Menggu Road, Zhabei, lost their six-year-old son, Yan Agan, on the 18th of this month. He speaks with a Huzhou accent, has a round face, and a mole in front of his right ear. He was wearing a small red hat, a gray-red cotton-padded jacket and pants. The Yan family reported the loss to the police station of the second precinct in the fifth district and requested an investigation, but there is still no trace of him. The Yan family is offering a reward of 100 yuan to find the child. Accusation Against an Unfilial Son

Gambling, Smoking, and Disobeying His Elderly Mother

The old Mrs. Xue Zhou, a woman from Gaoyou, lives at number 15, Xitan, Laobosheng Road, in the Shanghai West district. She is 51 years old and has been widowed for many years. She has a son named Bingquan, who is 28 years old. He was raised by her since childhood. She worked to make a living. After Bingquan grew up, she arranged for him to learn carpentry and, in 1926, arranged for him to marry a Sun woman from his hometown. Mrs. Xue thought that her son had a job and a family and that she could rely on him in her old age. Unexpectedly, Bingquan changed his ways soon after marrying. He abandoned his profession, became a vagrant, and often quarreled with his wife. As a result, Sun became resentful and developed an illness, eventually dying in the autumn of last year. From then on, Bingquan became even more absurd, gambling and smoking all day long. He accumulated debts and pawned everything. When his mother questioned him, he dared to speak harshly and was extremely unfilial. Recently, unable to borrow money, he demanded money from his elderly mother to support his smoking habit. If she refused, he would scold her. His mother could no longer bear it. Yesterday morning, while her son was lying on the bed at home, she snatched his opium pipe and lamp and, along with her son, reported the crime to the police station in the sixth district. After separate questioning by the district chief, who determined that the case involved idleness and disobedience to his elderly mother, a crime that could not be excused, he immediately prepared a document and sent him to the local court for trial.

Confiscation of Smuggled Opium

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Xinming" ship was returning to Shanghai from Tianjin. When the ship reached Tanggu, customs officers found a batch of smuggled opium hidden in the engine room. Customs officials confiscated the contraband and investigated the smuggler. The shipowner's investigation revealed that the opium was stolen and loaded by Lin Rui Da. Lin was not on the ship but was a helmsman on the Jiangjing ship. The Tianjin Customs fined the Xinming ship 1,000 taels of silver on the spot, and the ship was released. The shipowner was ordered to detain the opium offender and transfer him to court for prosecution. The shipping company has followed these instructions.
