Japanese Man Shoots Doorkeeper

At around 8:00 PM last night, an unexpected visitor, a Japanese man, arrived at the Sanyutou Foreign Company, a Japanese company at number 8, Nanxun Road, Hongkou. The doorkeeper, Shen Quanfu, (46 years old) asked him what he wanted. The man replied that he was there to meet the owner. Shen led him inside and asked him to wait downstairs while he informed the owner. Unexpectedly, the Japanese man insisted on going upstairs. When Shen refused, the man took out a handgun and fired a shot, hitting Shen in the lower abdomen. The bullet went through, and blood gushed out. The assailant then fled. People called Hua detectives 437 and 418, who hired a car to send Shen to Tongren Hospital for treatment. They also reported the incident to the Hongkou police station and requested an arrest.

Ministry of Railways Approves Bonuses for Staff on Two Railways

Result of Guo Chengen's Request to Beijing

According to the Ri Ri News Agency, staff on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways who have served for more than six months will be given bonuses by the management bureau at the end of each year as an incentive. This year, due to the financial situation of the two railway bureaus, the revenue and expenditure offset each other, leaving no surplus, making it impossible to allocate the bonuses. Staff on the two railways had repeatedly requested the bureau to issue the bonuses, but the issue was not resolved. Guo Chengen, director of the two railway bureaus, personally went to Beijing to present his views to the Ministry of Railways and request approval for the allocation. His request was approved by the Ministry of Railways, which agreed to allocate the funds. Guo returned to Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday and ordered the funds to be raised.

French Police Suppress Gatherings

The French police have specific regulations regarding group gatherings. The police must be notified in detail of the reasons for the gathering in advance. Only after it is verified that there is no other purpose will the meeting be allowed. However, recently, there have been cases of private gatherings under the guise of group activities, which are detrimental to the public security of the concession. According to the regulations for holding meetings in the French Concession, the French police must be notified 48 hours in advance, and a letter of permission must be obtained before the meeting can be convened. Otherwise, it will be considered a violation, and the person in charge will be detained and sent to court for punishment. The regulations for holding meetings in the French Concession are recorded below:

Order No. 45 of the French Consul General's Office in the Shanghai French Concession (Abolishing Order No. 6 of February 17, 1917) According to Article 13 of the organizational charter of the French Concession Public Works Bureau, the Consul General has decided as follows: (1) No political gathering, office, association, or any organization may be held or established in the French Concession without the permission of the French Consul General or his committee. (2) Anyone wishing to hold a similar gathering, establish a similar office, or form a similar association or organization within the concession must apply to the French police chief for permission at least 48 hours in advance. The application must report the purpose of the gathering, the agenda of the meeting, the composition of the participants, and provide detailed information on the constitution, or report the purpose of the association or organization and submit a list of the names of the responsible persons. (3) This order repeals Order No. 6 of February 17, 1917. May 3, 1927, Signed by Nazi, French Consul General in Shanghai.

News from Trade Associations

Biscuit, Candy, and Canned Goods Industry The Biscuit, Candy, and Canned Goods Industry Association issued a notice yesterday regarding the abolition of New Year's greetings, stating: "Notice: According to the proposal of Chairman Zhang Yichen at the general meeting of all member representatives of the association, it is hereby notified to all members that, as the New Year is approaching, at this time of national crisis, all New Year's greetings and all entertainment during the New Year should be abolished. Please decide whether this is appropriate." The general meeting resolved that, at this time of national crisis, with foreign aggression becoming more urgent and internal unrest continuing, there is no time for celebration. All New Year's greetings and all entertainment during the New Year should be abolished. Please send all expenses to the meeting to be remitted to aid disaster victims, to assist with good deeds, etc. In response, all manufacturers and shops are expected to comply with the decision and act accordingly. It is also reported that the association, due to the fact that the member company Hua Ji Confectionery Company was found by the Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau to have a number of unrelated delivery and order forms, which were deemed as disguised invoices evading stamp tax, was ordered to pay a fine of 300 yuan, and that the bureau also ignored letters from the association. The association believes that such excessive fines will cause great and undeserved losses to all shops in the city and has sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to raise objections to the Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau and to seriously negotiate in order to recover the fine, so as to fulfill its responsibility to protect merchants in difficult times.

Reader Correspondence

Mr. Zhou Cailiang's Message (The Responsibilities of Shop Assistants in Boycotting Japanese Goods)

Recently, the call for economic severance with Japan has spread throughout the country. If this matter can be sustained, it will be enough to deal a fatal blow to the Japanese invaders. However, the repeated failures of the past are truly heartbreaking. Therefore, how to plan for the future requires careful and thorough consideration. As a member of the business community, I would like to share my experience in service regarding the various responsibilities that should be fulfilled in boycotting Japanese goods, to encourage myself and inform my fellow countrymen, which is the so-called "doing what is within my power." (1) To manufacturers, we should use our daily service experience and customer feedback on domestic products to contribute to various domestic factories, so that they can improve based on the reports. We should also pay attention to substitutes for foreign goods at all times, and urge the government to carry out large-scale imitation. In this way, domestic goods will sell well, and foreign goods will be self-restricted without resistance. (2) To shop owners, the business community has made great progress in boycotting Japanese goods this time compared to the past, such as voluntarily sealing up and reporting, which is admirable. However, I have heard that there are still a few merchants who are blinded by greed and ignore the greater good, and even stoop to selling Japanese goods, or disguise them and vigorously promote them. Customers find it difficult to distinguish them, so it is easy to confuse them. Shop assistants, on the other hand, have more extensive access to information, and should use their patriotic conscience to make sincere advice. If they are still stubborn, then follow it up with weeping and pleading. If weeping and pleading are not effective, then there is no choice but to report them. Even if they lose their jobs as a result, they will surely gain social sympathy and be assisted. (3) To customers, at this time of national crisis and intense boycott of Japanese goods, customers will surely feel ashamed to buy enemy goods. If there are those who only seek cheapness and do not know what patriotism is, then we should tell them about the recent atrocities committed by the Japanese in our Eastern Provinces, and the reasons why our country has had to implement economic severance, so that they can awaken themselves and create opportunities to promote domestic goods. If they inquire about the types of products, we should answer them in detail, as this will not only win the goodwill of customers, but also greatly benefit business. (4) To ourselves, I have heard that those who wear foreign clothes while talking about loving and using domestic goods are ridiculed by everyone. Therefore, when shop assistants are promoting domestic goods, they should also examine themselves. It does not matter if old clothes are used, but if newly added clothes still contain enemy goods, it will not only fail to convince others, but also damage their own personality. As the saying goes, "The gentleman must first examine himself before he can ask of others." I sincerely hope that my fellow shop assistants will reflect on these words.

(Reply) If everything Mr. Zhou said is done, he can be considered a model shop assistant. Originally, this matter of boycotting Japanese goods mainly depends on the shop assistants. If it succeeds in the future, and when it comes to whose contribution is the greatest, someone will surely think that it is the contribution of the general shop assistants that is the greatest. Shop assistants, work hard, work hard.

Floral Imprint Communication

Affix this floral imprint and attach a corresponding amount of postage stamps when communicating.

Free Talk

Memories of Dailiang

— Yanzi

Since the standard of living in the world has increased, it is not only the Chinese who suffer, but also various countries in the East and West. Recently, I saw a foreign newspaper report on the plight of economic panic in Japan. The number of unemployed workers is increasing. The number of unemployed university graduates has reached 15,000. Even for female students, there are those who change to learning singing and playing instruments without graduating from specialized courses, wanting to become geishas. Thinking of this, I recall Shanghai thirty years ago. The area around Zhonghongqiao and Yalu Road was a gathering place for Japanese prostitutes. I occasionally drank with friends around the stove at the Apricot Blossom Pavilion. A guest once asked the manager about the procedure for calling a Japanese prostitute. The manager immediately presented a "Hundred Beauties Picture" for the guest to choose from. Generally, those who were ugly would sing well, and those who were beautiful would sing poorly. Each hour cost five "eagle wings" (silver coins). The prostitutes who sang well held a cow horn piece in their hands, plucked the strings, and sang loudly, but it was not very pleasant to listen to. However, the Japanese prostitutes were very strict in serving guests. Whoever called them would sit beside that person, and would not interact with the person sitting next to them. After a full hour, they would smile, bow, say goodbye, and leave, with absolutely no affectionate or coquettish attitude. It is said that the night fee was only doubled. Later, it was banned by the Japanese consulate, and since the Republic of China, we have not seen such people again.

The Story of a Confucian Official Fighting Against the Japanese

— Qiu Wenwei

I once read in the notes of a Ming dynasty person about the events of Ren Gong's resistance to the Japanese, and I was always moved and admired, and could not help myself. Ren Gong served as a county magistrate and deputy magistrate through the imperial examination, but he had never been in the military. However, in a moment of crisis, he generously accepted the order, expecting to die. He did not even want to say goodbye to his family. In the end, he was able to drive newly recruited soldiers, annihilate fierce bandits, defend the border and strengthen the garrison, and achieve considerable success. Seeing that he faced arrows and blades, and his body was covered with wounds, yet a Confucian official was able to do this, can he not be called a great man? Alas, the Northeast has fallen, and the people are suffering. The severity of the disaster is greater than that of the late Ming dynasty. However, those who hold high positions and possess heavy troops are losing power and land, harming the country and endangering the people, allowing foreign tribes to invade, and unable to add a single soldier or arrow. They are still cautious and hesitant, looking forward and backward, and must weigh the strength and weakness and predict the success or failure before going to war. Then, there will be no opportunity to fight forever. Therefore, I have extracted the old events of Ren Gong and narrated their outline, so that those who bear the responsibility of guarding the land may know what to learn from.

Ren Gong Huan, courtesy name Yingqian, was a native of Changzhi, Shanxi. He was a Jinshi in the 23rd year of Shizong. Nine years later, he became the County Magistrate of Di Su. In the intercalary March of the following year, Renzi, the Japanese alarm was first heard. At that time, there had been peace for a long time, and the soldiers suddenly rose up, shocking far and near. In April, the bandits attacked Taicang. Cai Zhongcheng ordered Gong to suppress them, giving him 300 soldiers, all newly recruited. Gong expected to die, without turning back. He did not enter to say goodbye to his family, but wrote a letter to them and left. He personally put on armor and went to battle. He encouraged the soldiers, and none dared to disobey. Gong followed the bandits' direction and set up defenses. He wore tattered clothes and straw sandals, and walked with the soldiers. When it rained, it was dark and there was no rest. He relied on grass, chewed dry provisions, and drank water, sharing the same hardships. He also exhorted them with ancient righteous deeds, so the soldiers submitted to his heart, and were willing to live and die with Gong. On the fifth day of the following year, Gui Chou, the bandits approached the city of Jiading. Gong and the Zhejiang Deputy General Lu Tang attacked together, agreeing to use fire as a signal. They advanced on all sides. The soldiers fought desperately, setting fire to kill them. The bandits charged away like pigs. Soon, the bandits spread throughout the inland. Gong traveled to Taicang, where all the bandits in the villages had gathered, encircling the city, and preparing siege equipment on three sides, intending to slaughter them. They approached with melee combat and climbed the city walls. Gong led the death squad to chop them with flying blades. Arrows and stones rained down, killing and wounding many. The bandits initially thought that we were easy to deal with and that the city could be taken in the morning and evening. At this point, they began to fear. In the first month of Jia Yin, the bandits captured Chongde and attacked Wujiang. The Inspector Zhou Gong Rudou ordered Gong to supervise Yu Dayou and other armies to attack Shengdun in a pincer movement, killing three thousand. They attacked Miaohu, killing seventy-three. The bandits' momentum was greatly weakened. In May, they returned to Lujing. Gong fought fiercely with them on the dam. From Chen to Shen, the bandits were routed, beheading eight hundred, almost wiping them out. But Gong hurriedly returned home barefoot because of the taboo of mourning. He was devastated by his grief, and because he had previously fought without regard for his own safety, he faced arrows and blades, and his body was covered with wounds, he fell seriously ill. He died not long after.

Trivial Talks

— Zui Chi Sheng

Raising a Cat is Not as Good as Feeding Mice A certain Jia neighbor raised a cat. At first, he loved it very much. However, the cat was full, ate well, slept soundly, and let the mice run rampant. It also often left excrement on the couch or stole food from the kitchen. Even the goldfish raised in the courtyard were often consumed by it. Jia was furious and said, "I provide fish and meat every day to feed the cat, hoping that it can eliminate the mice. Now, not only does it not catch mice, but it is even more troublesome than the mice. What use do I have for such a cat?" So he drove it away and did not raise cats anymore. Instead, he placed a small amount of rice in the dark corners every day to feed the mice. When he looked at it in the morning, there were no grains of rice left. The mice seemed to know his kindness, and since then, they have not been harmful to people. Jia once told people about this, saying, "I treated the cat well, but the cat did not know how to do its duty. I feed the mice, and the cost is minimal, and it can turn out to be harmless to people. Therefore, 'Raising a cat is not as good as feeding mice.'" Those who heard this passed it around as a joke.

A White Turtle The Shanghai dialect uses "white turtle" to mean "goose." It is not true that turtles are white. Unexpectedly, I have seen a white turtle. I remember in August this year, one evening, I took a leisurely walk across the Nine-Turn Bridge in the Town God Temple Yu Garden. I leaned on the railing and looked down at the swimming fish. Someone next to me said in surprise, "A white turtle." I looked closely and saw a giant turtle floating on the surface of the water. Its whole body was white, and its head, tail, feet, and claws were all white. Later, I passed by the place, but I never saw it again. It is not surprising to see a white sparrow, but I don't know if this white turtle is also a rare object. I specifically record it to ask experts. Also, a certain amusement park in this city once had a white turtle on display for people to see. I don't know what its shape is like or where it came from. I should explore it when I have time.

World Tidbits

The Reason for Female Longevity There is an old lady in Scotland who is one hundred years old. She is still very healthy. Someone asked her the reason for her longevity. She said, "The reason why women live long is because they are more gentle by nature and are always calm."

The Healthiest Place in the World No matter how hygienic any country in the world is, it cannot reach the healthiest state. The healthiest place on the entire planet is the Antarctic region. Any kind of microorganism and germ cannot live there.

High Stools in Photography Studios In several film company photography studios in Hollywood, America, there are several very high stools specially for female stars to sit on. This is because they often wear long skirts when performing. Sitting on high stools can prevent the skirts from touching the ground and getting dirty.

A Clever Way to Stop Smuggling On the border between the Netherlands and Germany, people often smuggle car oil and rubber tires in cars. As they pass by at a glance, the German authorities have specially made a kind of wooden board. The board is full of iron clusters. Throwing it on the road will prevent vehicles from passing.

Going to War

— A Member of the Youth Aid Horse Regiment

(Nine) Leaving Zhenjiang

We stayed in Zhenjiang for two whole days. Everyone's spirit was rejuvenated by this long period of rest and was as vigorous as usual. So we moved forward again.

On the afternoon of the 18th, we said goodbye to the students in Zhenjiang and left Zhenjiang by car. All the way, we only heard the rumbling of the rails, which was very similar to the sound of guns and cannons heard when sitting in an armored car on the front line. The vast fields outside the window were spinning by non-stop. Isn't everything in the universe progressing endlessly like this? However, I feel that the current state of our country is in danger of stopping its progress. Perhaps this is the reason why the Japanese invaders are encroaching on us.

At about five o'clock, we were about to reach Nanjing Station. As we passed the foreign flag, the car suddenly stopped. Then, a locomotive came and towed the car we were sitting in away from the train and onto another track. After a short time, it pulled up next to a platform. Not only were there no people welcoming us at the station, but there was not a single passenger to be seen. The residents next to the station were only a few low houses covered with straw. On the left side of the car, there were three or five iron-covered freight cars. The scene was very desolate. At this time, it was dusk, and combined with the short days of this winter season, it was already difficult to see anything clearly. I only saw many masts not far from the car window. These things made me suspicious. Could it be that the government is cracking down on us? I thought. My mind was guessing wildly. Just then, the leader of the group arrived. I could no longer bear it and finally asked the leader of the group. I learned that the Nanjing Garrison Command had sent the students from various places in Beijing back to their schools. It was feared that the students would use the excuse of welcoming us and refuse to go back. Therefore, the authorities did not let outsiders know about our arrival in Beijing. In order to avoid attention, they simply moved our vehicles to this riverside station. Therefore, we understood the government's difficulties and spent the night in the car that night.

We slept in the car, which was the first time since we set off. Although we didn't sleep as comfortably as we did when we were at Zhenjiang Middle School, we were in a carriage filled with the smell of representatives from various provinces, especially with brothers who were determined to go to the national crisis together. Our eyes were drawn to the people from the various provinces and cities. Our hearts were competing with each other for the courage to kill the enemy in the future. As a result, the elements of our friendship increased, and the spirit of destroying the Japanese became stronger.

On the 19th, we were still in the car. I don't know how the students of Jinling University had learned about our news. They sent representatives to contact us about welcome matters. We can probably stay in the Jinling University school building tomorrow night.

Remarks on the National Crisis Relief Painting and Calligraphy Exhibition

— He Tianjian

The national crisis is urgent! The violent Japanese army has occupied our Eastern Provinces and has launched an attack on Jinzhou. If Jinzhou is lost, then Pingjin will be in danger. If Pingjin is in danger, then our southeastern provinces will be directly threatened. Therefore, if we want to seek relief at this time, there are still some days left. After this, I am afraid that there will be no more opportunities for us to calmly plan. Although our painters and calligraphers each pride themselves on individualism, when it comes to the loss of the country and the destruction of the nation, their suffering is no different from that of others. Ms. He Xiangning has just returned from Western Europe and initiated a National Crisis Relief Painting and Calligraphy Exhibition. Painters and calligraphers on the sea were all invited to participate. For a time, the response was like a myriad of streams flowing into the sea. Ms. He's admiration reaches this point. Or is it that people who are united in overcoming the national crisis have the same heart? With my incompetence, I will also attach myself to the tail of a good horse. In the face of great difficulties, everyone is responsible. Who can bear not to do it? This is indeed my ambition, and I have expressed it again and again. It's just that because of the delay, it has not been realized. The conference recommended Mr. Wang Yingbin and me to be in charge of publicity. Although I am incompetent, I have no choice but to try my best in the face of the great cause. The results of the ticket sales were exceptionally satisfactory. The efforts of Mr. Zheng Hongnian and Mr. Ye Gongchuo were instrumental in achieving this. The collection of works was carried out by Mr. Liu Haisu and Mr. Qian Shoutie, and the results exceeded the expected amount. However, without Ms. He Xiangning, Mr. Zhu Shaoping, and Mr. Liu Yazi's calm arrangements, it would not have been easy to achieve such results. As for the layout of the venue, Mr. Sun Xueni and Mr. Xue Baolun were responsible for it. They are experienced and capable. The opening should give us an impression of orderliness. The works added this time are all carefully crafted masterpieces by famous artists. I also have some humble works added. How could I not know to avoid the suspicion of showing off? Gold leaping out of the furnace is considered strange. I certainly don't want that either. However, publicity is involved, so I cannot stop eating because of choking. Perhaps it will also be understood by connoisseurs. In the future, if we fight bravely and rescue someone, so that the mountains and rivers are returned to us and the golden goblet is not missing, the people of the country will have contributed to it. Will its achievements be solely attributed to us painters and calligraphers?

Talks on Pink and Black

— Peilan

The entire play "Yutang Chun" comes from Shaanxi Bangzi. The Erhuang Qingyi initially did not practice this. When I was young, I listened to the singing of the opera troupe. "Yutang Chun" was rarely seen. Occasionally, it was performed by Bangzi Qingyi. At that time, only Tian'e Dan, Sizhan Deng, Boli Cui, and Xiao Jinwa were considered excellent. The audience did not pay much attention to this play, and it was not as popular as "Burning Bones," "Willow Forest Pond," "Three Suspicion Plan," or "Biographies of Martyrs." The famous Erhuang Qingyi predecessors, such as Xi Luyi, Yun Shitou, Chang Zihe, and others, were never seen singing "Yutang Chun." Feng Zihe was known for being both a Zheng Gong Qingyi and a Huadan and enjoyed a great reputation at one time, but he never became famous for "Yutang Chun." During the era when the New Stage moved to the Sixteenth Pier, Zihe and Mao Yunke both belonged there. Occasionally, they performed the entire play "Yutang Chun" during the day. Zihe only sang the section "Hongtong is Falsely Accused." The "Escort" and "Joint Trial" were all taken up by Yunke. Yunke was originally a Bangzi singer. Later, someone changed the "Escort" and "Joint Trial" sections into Erhuang. As a result, almost all Qingyi and Huashan singers in the north and south sang these two plays. When Mei Lanfang and Cheng Yanqiu emerged, "Yutang Chun" became even more popular. Yanqiu, through the transmission of Yao Qing, sang a new tune. Those who imitated it intensified their efforts. Although the old rules were gradually lost, the music lovers never tired of listening to it. However, the scenes before the escort, such as the three brothels, temple fairs, giving silver, and Hongtong being falsely accused, are still the old rules of Bangzi. When Xun Huisheng and Xu Biyun succeeded, the entire play "Yutang Chun" was sung by one person from beginning to end. As a result, the entire play was changed to Erhuang, and the Bangzi face disappeared completely. Xu Biyun can be ignored, but Xun Huisheng's "Yutang Chun" was also very exciting in the first half. I especially love the Nanbangzi in the "Making Up" scene. The lyrics are elegant and refined, and the tune is clever and beautiful. The graceful and charming singing moves the heart. Beikai Company has included this section in a record. Those who love to watch "Yutang Chun" can try to listen to it.

Casual Talks from the Tixiang Zhai

— Cheng Dequan

In the upheaval of the Xinhai Revolution, those in the know already knew that the Qing Dynasty was doomed to perish. Most of the governors and governors abandoned their cities and fled. Only three people, the Governor of Fujian Songshou, the Governor of Shanxi Lu Zhongqi, and the Governor of Jiangxi Feng Ruzhen, sacrificed themselves to the festival. There were also three people who surrendered: the Governor of Shandong Sun Baoqi, the Governor of Guangxi Shen Bingkun, and the Governor of Jiangsu Cheng Dequan. Among these three, Baoqi changed in the middle, and Bingkun was forced. Only Dequan's rebellion was the earliest, and he was also the first to become governor. He was also appointed commander-in-chief of the allied Jiangsu and Zhejiang forces attacking Jiangning. Because of this, he was especially trusted by the great men of the founding of the country, while the old officials ridiculed him for his disloyalty. There is no right or wrong, merit or crime in the world, which has been the case since ancient times. Dequan's abandonment of the governorship to become governor, the name is different but the substance remains. The politics of democracy and the system of autocracy are completely different. There is no such thing as a traitor. Those who understand the times are outstanding. Dequan's desire not to end his political career did not ask whether the political system was democratic or monarchical, or whether the official position was governor or governor. This is clear. Dequan, courtesy name Xuelou, was a native of Rongyang, Sichuan. He was a Lin Gongsheng. He paid tribute grain to become a Second Yin and served in Anhui. Someone hated the inspecting censor Zhao Erxun for something and made a couplet to satirize him: "You are a petty scholar, born to be mean. Xun cuts off below, cutting off your descendants." Erxun was angry and did not know who had played the prank. Coincidentally, Dequan came to visit. Erxun told him. The remaining anger had not subsided. Dequan said, "I have also heard something and have changed the wording to 'You are a petty scholar, born with integrity. Xun cuts off below, cutting off no emotion.' It is truly because you are pure in nature and enforce the law like a mountain, that I thought of this. Although it is not well-written, it is still relevant." Erxun smiled and said, "It is enough to see that justice still exists in people's hearts. Your talent and learning can be seen from this." So they became friends. Later, Erxun became the General of Fengtian. Dequan had already been there first and had been promoted to the rank of prefect. Erxun repeatedly recommended his talents and was promoted from a Daoyuan to a Deputy Commander. He was acting General of Heilongjiang. When the three eastern provinces changed their ways, he asked for leave and left. He was re-appointed as the Governor of Fengtian. His political views were not in agreement with the Governor-General Xiliang. He sought other transfers, but could not get them. Suddenly, he came up with a plan. Because the Governor and Governor-General were in the same office, the Governor-General was in charge of the political power, and the Governor had nothing to do. He requested that the post be abolished. The report was approved. Liang was shocked and asked Dequan, "You wrote a memorial to the court, and the governor acted privately, secretly without letting me know. Why?" Dequan replied, "The abolition of the post, the abolition of my own post. If I ask for your approval, the Governor-General will definitely keep me. If I am kept, then the post cannot be abolished. If the post is not abolished, then my determination to retire cannot be fulfilled." Liang had no way to argue with him and dismissed it with a smile. After a little while, the decree to govern Jiangsu was issued. Liang realized how clever Dequan was in his official career. In the first year of the Republic, the provisional government was established in Nanjing. Dequan was selected to be in charge of the Ministry of Internal Affairs. He followed the great men of the time every day and seemed to regard himself as a founding hero. When discussing a certain matter, Dequan was about to leave the meeting. The person sitting with him accused him of a great injustice. He ignored it and left. The next day, when discussing the matter again, he falsely claimed to have a sudden illness and could not speak because his throat was hoarse. In the evening, someone met him at Tang Shaoyi's seat. Dequan was talking eloquently. Zhongshan heard about it and sighed, "Such a person cannot be conspired with." At that time, there was a mutiny in Wumen. Governor Zhuang Yunkuan requested to be dismissed. Chen Qimei said that Dequan was familiar with the local situation and could be reinstated. Dequan then took up military command again. During the Gui Chou campaign against Yuan, he raised the banner of independence. When he failed, he secretly telegraphed Xiangcheng, saying that he had been forced to do so and that it was not his own intention. Xiangcheng looked at the telegram and laughed, "Xuelou will be finished from now on." From then on for more than ten years, he wore a cassock, held classics in his hand, and recited Amitabha Buddha every day. In a certain year, he died in Shanghai. His last words were to be buried in monk's clothes, probably with the intention of repentance. A certain old man said that he became a Buddha after descending to earth, which is a joke.

A Letter from the Common People to the Soldiers (Part 1)

— Common People

Armed officers and soldiers, compatriots.

Before I speak, let me make clear my position and yours.

I am one of the people of the Republic of China. I am a citizen who bears national taxes and local taxes. I am the master of the country. I am a commoner who works 365 days a year without rest. You eat what we commoners eat, and wear what we commoners wear. You neither farm, nor work, nor do business. You enjoy material things much more comfortably than we commoners. Have you ever thought that you were born with a good fate to be able to survive without labor? We take the blood and sweat of generations and pay the price to support you. You receive our support. Have you ever thought about how to be worthy of us? Perhaps some of you who understand a little will say, "We are the national army. It is true that we are supported by the blood and sweat of the common people. But we are protecting the common people and defending the country. We are killing the enemy for the common people..." Since this is the case, please forgive my bluntness. I want to say a few words from the position of the common people. In peacetime, when internal wars that can lead to the destruction of the country occur, the newspapers are full of telegrams asking to fight against the rebels, waiting for orders with swords as pillows, and hating the enemy together. How admirable! The battles of Nankou and Wuchang created world-shaking achievements. How admirable is this! What about now? The violent Japanese have invaded our homes, and the voices of co-managing China are singing to the clouds again. When I open the newspaper and take a look, how many people are asking to fight against the thieves, how many are waiting for orders with swords as pillows, and how many more hate the enemy together? It almost makes us commoners suspect that this flood has washed all the brave soldiers who fought so hard in the previous civil wars to the iceberg. They are freezing and pitiful and cannot even say a word. Is the land of the three eastern provinces not Chinese? Do the people of the three eastern provinces not bear military expenses? You are the national army. Should you not care about the affairs of the three eastern provinces and not protect the people of the three eastern provinces? Are you really defending the country and killing the enemy for the common people? Thinking of the pain that the common people bear

and the reality of this event, tears cannot help but flow into my heart. Armed compatriots, how can you be worthy of the common people?

Financial and Gold Market Situation Calm

No Strong Fluctuations　Yesterday the Gold Exchange already opened; the bullion market situation was still calm. However, sentiment among traders was initially high and then softened, so the market price rose and then fell, with a total difference of thirteen taels between countries throughout the day. Ultimately, there was a slight increase of one or two taels. The initial opening was high, likely because the silver bars saw a slight increase during this Christmas holiday. American silver showed no improvement or decline. With active buying, it quickly broke through 680 taels. Foreign exchange seemed to strengthen, but later in the session, although there was hedging, many people were looking for cash, so it kept falling, especially with the loosening of drafts, causing a sharp drop of more than ten taels. The later market trended slightly milder but had some fluctuation, with the final calculation at 676-677 taels. However, because it is the end of the lunar year, neither the bulls nor the bears had much volume to trade. Dafengheng had previously pledged to short positions, using Kangtie to advance 11.5 yuan.

Early Market Turned from High to Low　From the early opening, it immediately rose four taels to 679 taels. Silver bars on the 25th only rose by one-sixteenth, with no market on the 26th and 27th. American silver showed no change, so sentiment was good. Tianfenyong and others were the first to buy, rising from 78.5 taels to 83.5 taels. Soon after, Chunyuanyong and hedgers sold, and Mitsui offered March US dollars at $33.625, immediately falling five or six taels to 77.5 yuan. HSBC offered January British gold at 11 pence 6875, and Sumitomo offered March US dollars at $33.625. Then retail buyers came in, adding a little more than one or two taels. British gold quotations remained the same, ranging from nine to eight and a half taels. Suddenly, Mumbai came to buy British gold for March at half a penny, and Qian Changxiang, Fuyu, and others competed to buy, so the market situation soared, rising six or seven taels to 85 taels at 10:00 AM. Suddenly, it was heard that HSBC sold March US dollars at 625, and banks mutually traded spot British gold at 625 and spot US dollars at 75. Furthermore, Fuchang and other hedgers sold, with Hengyu, Zhifengyong, Yifengyong, Yongtong, Taichang, Yongfeng, Yuamoyu, and others successively selling, resulting in a drop of six taels. At 10:30 AM, it was 79 taels. At that time, Mumbai bought US dollars at 625 again, and retail investors bought, adding two taels to 81 taels. By 11:00 AM, there was a renewed sign of weakness. Yu Dayuan, Maoyong, Dadecheng, Yifengyong, Yongfeng, and others all sold, and March US dollars were matched at 6875, and then 75 could be settled, and British gold at 625, leading to a continuous decline in the gold price. At 11:15 AM, it was 74 taels. Japanese banks mutually traded March US dollars at 875. Afterwards, Hengyu and Taichang slightly advanced, raising it by three taels to 72 yuan. By 11:30 AM, buyers were widespread, so the price was unsustainable, and it quickly retreated by more than five taels. The noon closing was only calculated at 71.8 yuan, re-doing to 73 taels, and then reverting to more than 71 taels. The quoted price was still 725 taels, with an estimated squeeze of around 50 taels.

Afternoon Turned Milder　The afternoon market opened at 71.5 taels. Later, because Zhifengyong, Yongtong, Taichang, Cuichangyong, and others bought, and February US dollars could be sold at $34, and then Japanese merchants mutually traded spot at $4, it reached 75.8 taels at 2:30 PM. Suddenly, it depreciated by two taels, and retail investors sold. It then rose again, with Tongtaichang, Qianchangxiang, Hongkangyong, Zhifengyong, and others coming to pay. In particular, banks mutually traded April British gold at 5625, Datong sold January 6875 to HSBC, and Huabi offered March at 11 pence, making the market firm, reaching 78.8 taels after 3:30 PM. Later, from 3:30 PM to 4:15 PM, the trend softened because Yuanmaoyong, Hengchangyong, Taifengcheng, and goods came to sell, resulting in a drop of four taels, with slight fluctuations of one or two taels in between. It then became 74.5 taels, then adding two taels, with short positions covering. At 4:30 PM, the closing price was 76 taels, and then it was rushed to 78 taels, adding one tael compared to the 24th (according to the listed price). According to the full day, the maximum price was 85 taels, and the minimum was 71.5 taels, a difference of 13.5 taels. Goods in the early morning were 79 taels, at noon it was 1.5 taels, in the afternoon it was 1.2 yuan, and the closing was 8 taels. The quoted price was an estimated squeeze of 50 taels, recorded at 82 taels, 72 taels to replenish water at 79 taels, 83 taels in the afternoon, and the red bar was calculated to add 15 taels.

Zhifengyong, Yuanmaoyong, Hengyu, Yuantai, Futaiheng, Tongtaichang, etc., came in and out intermittently. Dadecheng, Yifengyong, Yuanheng, Fuchang, and Yu Da all exited. Foreign Exchange Hovering

Hedgers Leaving at Only 25-27 Taels

From the 25th to yesterday, British silver only increased slightly by 0.0625, and American silver showed no prosperity or decline. Exchange rates rose and fell again, and the market situation was quite flat. Yesterday's HSBC listing, except for the French franc adding four yuan, the rest remained the same. Banks Opening and Closing with Heavy Settlement

The silver interest rate is high due to more money received.

Foreign funds are particularly busy due to government bond delivery.

Market Overview　Yesterday was the first day of opening for banks after the holidays. Three days' worth of settlements were processed in one day, and it was also the end of the year, so it was even busier. However, due to government bond delivery yesterday, it was slightly less than usual, but still busy. The high interest rate was due to excessive money received, with no other major key factor.

(Silver interest) The early market was 3 yuan 8 fen, and the noon market was 3 yuan, a sharp increase of about 2 li from the previous day. Head allocation plus water was 8-9 fen, and the bank listing was 1 yuan 5 fen.

Starting in March, the standard issue will be expanded, and all Chinese cotton can be delivered, so industry insiders mostly sold, and the market will be loose.

Hardware 200-Pound Association Iron Is Short and the Price Is Firm

The 200-pound Association iron is a hot-selling product for tobacco companies, canning factories, biscuit companies, and lard shops. Since the market was flooded with goods in the autumn, the standards have fallen back. In recent days, export merchants have frequently inquired about it, and hoarders have wanted to collect it because of the scarcity of goods and high costs, so the market air is good and the standards are likely to soar straight up. The current market price for old steel factory goods is 27 taels, and new steel factory goods are 26 taels 5 qian. As for the hard French goods, they are only 14 taels 5 qian, and the market also calls for 25 taels because of high costs, but its transactions, except for large cigarette boxes and at least biscuit cans, can not be used for cigarette cans and pig cans. According to foreign firms, imports of new and old 200-pound steel factory goods have been very deserted recently, and there is a prospect of progress in the future market.

Social News Submission Guidelines

(1) Texts limited to news about internal and external science, industry, commerce, and rural areas; (2) Hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life; (3) Photographs limited to youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, drama performances, lectures, gatherings, exhibitions, and various competitions), school news, and youth sports; individuals and groups are welcome to submit; do not write on both sides of the paper.

(4) Each text should not exceed 2,000 words.

(5) Write horizontally and do not write carelessly; Western text should be omitted as much as possible; if it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, do not write the characters carelessly, and do not write the characters carelessly. Western text should be omitted as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink, and do not use colored paper; use black for white paper.

(8) Please indicate "Youth World Editorial Department Collection" when submitting manuscripts.

(9) All submissions will not be returned whether they are published or not. If you need to return them, you should declare in advance and attach a stamped envelope.

(10) Remuneration for texts is 3 yuan, 2 yuan, and 1 yuan per thousand words; pictures and photos are also the same for each piece; for special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.

Book and Newspaper Introduction Submission Guidelines

(1) Texts are limited to introducing the latest domestic and foreign publications. All books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc., are included in the introduction except for literary works.

(2) Pictures are limited to the latest works of domestic and foreign new writers and illustrations related to the text.

(3) Texts on annotations or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) Each text should not exceed 3,000 words.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink, and do not use colored paper; use black for white paper.

(8) Please indicate "Book and Newspaper Introduction Editor Collection" when submitting manuscripts.

(9) All submissions will not be returned whether they are published or not. If you need to return them, you should declare in advance and attach a stamped envelope.

(10) Remuneration for texts is 3 yuan, 2 yuan, and 1 yuan per thousand words; pictures and photos are also the same for each piece; for special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.
